      99              : /*
     100              :  * Create a trigger.  Returns the address of the created trigger.
     101              :  *
     102              :  * queryString is the source text of the CREATE TRIGGER command.
     103              :  * This must be supplied if a whenClause is specified, else it can be NULL.
     104              :  *
     105              :  * relOid, if nonzero, is the relation on which the trigger should be
     106              :  * created.  If zero, the name provided in the statement will be looked up.
     107              :  *
     108              :  * refRelOid, if nonzero, is the relation to which the constraint trigger
     109              :  * refers.  If zero, the constraint relation name provided in the statement
     110              :  * will be looked up as needed.
     111              :  *
     112              :  * constraintOid, if nonzero, says that this trigger is being created
     113              :  * internally to implement that constraint.  A suitable pg_depend entry will
     114              :  * be made to link the trigger to that constraint.  constraintOid is zero when
     115              :  * executing a user-entered CREATE TRIGGER command.  (For CREATE CONSTRAINT
     116              :  * TRIGGER, we build a pg_constraint entry internally.)
     117              :  *
     118              :  * indexOid, if nonzero, is the OID of an index associated with the constraint.
     119              :  * We do nothing with this except store it into pg_trigger.tgconstrindid;
     120              :  * but when creating a trigger for a deferrable unique constraint on a
     121              :  * partitioned table, its children are looked up.  Note we don't cope with
     122              :  * invalid indexes in that case.
     123              :  *
     124              :  * funcoid, if nonzero, is the OID of the function to invoke.  When this is
     125              :  * given, stmt->funcname is ignored.
     126              :  *
     127              :  * parentTriggerOid, if nonzero, is a trigger that begets this one; so that
     128              :  * if that trigger is dropped, this one should be too.  (This is passed as
     129              :  * Invalid by most callers; it's set here when recursing on a partition.)
     130              :  *
     131              :  * If whenClause is passed, it is an already-transformed expression for
     132              :  * WHEN.  In this case, we ignore any that may come in stmt->whenClause.
     133              :  *
     134              :  * If isInternal is true then this is an internally-generated trigger.
     135              :  * This argument sets the tgisinternal field of the pg_trigger entry, and
     136              :  * if true causes us to modify the given trigger name to ensure uniqueness.
     137              :  *
     138              :  * When isInternal is not true we require ACL_TRIGGER permissions on the
     139              :  * relation, as well as ACL_EXECUTE on the trigger function.  For internal
     140              :  * triggers the caller must apply any required permission checks.
     141              :  *
     142              :  * When called on partitioned tables, this function recurses to create the
     143              :  * trigger on all the partitions, except if isInternal is true, in which
     144              :  * case caller is expected to execute recursion on its own.
     145              :  */

    3217              : /* ----------
    3218              :  * After-trigger stuff
    3219              :  *
    3220              :  * The AfterTriggersData struct holds data about pending AFTER trigger events
    3221              :  * during the current transaction tree.  (BEFORE triggers are fired
    3222              :  * immediately so we don't need any persistent state about them.)  The struct
    3223              :  * and most of its subsidiary data are kept in TopTransactionContext; however
    3224              :  * some data that can be discarded sooner appears in the CurTransactionContext
    3225              :  * of the relevant subtransaction.  Also, the individual event records are
    3226              :  * kept in a separate sub-context of TopTransactionContext.  This is done
    3227              :  * mainly so that it's easy to tell from a memory context dump how much space
    3228              :  * is being eaten by trigger events.
    3229              :  *
    3230              :  * Because the list of pending events can grow large, we go to some
    3231              :  * considerable effort to minimize per-event memory consumption.  The event
    3232              :  * records are grouped into chunks and common data for similar events in the
    3233              :  * same chunk is only stored once.
    3234              :  *
    3235              :  * XXX We need to be able to save the per-event data in a file if it grows too
    3236              :  * large.
    3237              :  * ----------
    3238              :  */
    3239              :

    3270              : 
    3271              : /*
    3272              :  * Per-trigger-event data
    3273              :  *
    3274              :  * The actual per-event data, AfterTriggerEventData, includes DONE/IN_PROGRESS
    3275              :  * status bits and up to two tuple CTIDs.  Each event record also has an
    3276              :  * associated AfterTriggerSharedData that is shared across all instances of
    3277              :  * similar events within a "chunk".
    3278              :  *
    3279              :  * For row-level triggers, we arrange not to waste storage on unneeded ctid
    3280              :  * fields.  Updates of regular tables use two; inserts and deletes of regular
    3281              :  * tables use one; foreign tables always use zero and save the tuple(s) to a
    3282              :  * tuplestore.  AFTER_TRIGGER_FDW_FETCH directs AfterTriggerExecute() to
    3283              :  * retrieve a fresh tuple or pair of tuples from that tuplestore, while
    3284              :  * AFTER_TRIGGER_FDW_REUSE directs it to use the most-recently-retrieved
    3285              :  * tuple(s).  This permits storing tuples once regardless of the number of
    3286              :  * row-level triggers on a foreign table.
    3287              :  *
    3288              :  * Note that we need triggers on foreign tables to be fired in exactly the
    3289              :  * order they were queued, so that the tuples come out of the tuplestore in
    3290              :  * the right order.  To ensure that, we forbid deferrable (constraint)
    3291              :  * triggers on foreign tables.  This also ensures that such triggers do not
    3292              :  * get deferred into outer trigger query levels, meaning that it's okay to
    3293              :  * destroy the tuplestore at the end of the query level.
    3294              :  *
    3295              :  * Statement-level triggers always bear AFTER_TRIGGER_1CTID, though they
    3296              :  * require no ctid field.  We lack the flag bit space to neatly represent that
    3297              :  * distinct case, and it seems unlikely to be worth much trouble.
    3298              :  *
    3299              :  * Note: ats_firing_id is initially zero and is set to something else when
    3300              :  * AFTER_TRIGGER_IN_PROGRESS is set.  It indicates which trigger firing
    3301              :  * cycle the trigger will be fired in (or was fired in, if DONE is set).
    3302              :  * Although this is mutable state, we can keep it in AfterTriggerSharedData
    3303              :  * because all instances of the same type of event in a given event list will
    3304              :  * be fired at the same time, if they were queued between the same firing
    3305              :  * cycles.  So we need only ensure that ats_firing_id is zero when attaching
    3306              :  * a new event to an existing AfterTriggerSharedData record.
    3307              :  */

    3410              : /*
    3411              :  * All per-transaction data for the AFTER TRIGGERS module.

    3417              :  * tell which ones to work on.  This ensures sane behavior if a trigger
    3418              :  * function chooses to do SET CONSTRAINTS: the inner SET CONSTRAINTS will
    3419              :  * only fire those events that weren't already scheduled for firing.
    3420              :  *
    3421              :  * state keeps track of the transaction-local effects of SET CONSTRAINTS.
    3422              :  * This is saved and restored across failed subtransactions.
    3423              :  *
    3424              :  * events is the current list of deferred events.  This is global across
    3425              :  * all subtransactions of the current transaction.  In a subtransaction
    3426              :  * abort, we know that the events added by the subtransaction are at the
    3427              :  * end of the list, so it is relatively easy to discard them.  The event
    3428              :  * list chunks themselves are stored in event_cxt.
    3429              :  *
    3430              :  * query_depth is the current depth of nested AfterTriggerBeginQuery calls
    3431              :  * (-1 when the stack is empty).
    3432              :  *
    3433              :  * query_stack[query_depth] is the per-query-level data, including these fields:
    3434              :  *
    3435              :  * events is a list of AFTER trigger events queued by the current query.
    3436              :  * None of these are valid until the matching AfterTriggerEndQuery call
    3437              :  * occurs.  At that point we fire immediate-mode triggers, and append any
    3438              :  * deferred events to the main events list.
    3439              :  *
    3440              :  * fdw_tuplestore is a tuplestore containing the foreign-table tuples
    3441              :  * needed by events queued by the current query.  (Note: we use just one
    3442              :  * tuplestore even though more than one foreign table might be involved.
    3443              :  * This is okay because tuplestores don't really care what's in the tuples
    3444              :  * they store; but it's possible that someday it'd break.)
    3445              :  *
    3446              :  * tables is a List of AfterTriggersTableData structs for target tables
    3447              :  * of the current query (see below).
    3448              :  *
    3449              :  * maxquerydepth is just the allocated length of query_stack.
    3450              :  *
    3451              :  * trans_stack holds per-subtransaction data, including these fields:
    3452              :  *
    3453              :  * state is NULL or a pointer to a saved copy of the SET CONSTRAINTS
    3454              :  * state data.  Each subtransaction level that modifies that state first
    3455              :  * saves a copy, which we use to restore the state if we abort.
    3456              :  *
    3457              :  * events is a copy of the events head/tail pointers,
    3458              :  * which we use to restore those values during subtransaction abort.
    3459              :  *
    3460              :  * query_depth is the subtransaction-start-time value of query_depth,
    3461              :  * which we similarly use to clean up at subtransaction abort.
    3462              :  *
    3463              :  * firing_counter is the subtransaction-start-time value of firing_counter.
    3464              :  * We use this to recognize which deferred triggers were fired (or marked
    3465              :  * for firing) within an aborted subtransaction.
    3466              :  *
    3467              :  * We use GetCurrentTransactionNestLevel() to determine the correct array
    3468              :  * index in trans_stack.  maxtransdepth is the number of allocated entries in
    3469              :  * trans_stack.  (By not keeping our own stack pointer, we can avoid trouble
    3470              :  * in cases where errors during subxact abort cause multiple invocations
    3471              :  * of AfterTriggerEndSubXact() at the same nesting depth.)
    3472              :  *
    3473              :  * We create an AfterTriggersTableData struct for each target table of the
    3474              :  * current query, and each operation mode (INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE), that has
    3475              :  * either transition tables or statement-level triggers.  This is used to
    3476              :  * hold the relevant transition tables, as well as info tracking whether
    3477              :  * we already queued the statement triggers.  (We use that info to prevent
    3478              :  * firing the same statement triggers more than once per statement, or really
    3479              :  * once per transition table set.)  These structs, along with the transition
    3480              :  * table tuplestores, live in the (sub)transaction's CurTransactionContext.
    3481              :  * That's sufficient lifespan because we don't allow transition tables to be
    3482              :  * used by deferrable triggers, so they only need to survive until
    3483              :  * AfterTriggerEndQuery.
    3484              :  */
    3485              : typedef struct AfterTriggersQueryData AfterTriggersQueryData;
    3486              : typedef struct AfterTriggersTransData AfterTriggersTransData;
    3487              : typedef struct AfterTriggersTableData AfterTriggersTableData;
    3488              : 
    3489              : typedef struct AfterTriggersData
    3490              : {
    3491              :         CommandId       firing_counter; /* next firing ID to assign */
    3492              :         SetConstraintState state;       /* the active S C state */
    3493              :         AfterTriggerEventList events;   /* deferred-event list */
    3494              :         MemoryContext event_cxt;        /* memory context for events, if any */
    3495              : 
    3496              :         /* per-query-level data: */

    3500              :

    5409              : /* ----------
    5410              :  * AfterTriggerPendingOnRel()
    5411              :  *              Test to see if there are any pending after-trigger events for rel.
    5412              :  *
    5413              :  * This is used by TRUNCATE, CLUSTER, ALTER TABLE, etc to detect whether
    5414              :  * it is unsafe to perform major surgery on a relation.  Note that only
    5415              :  * local pending events are examined.  We assume that having exclusive lock

    5852              :  * statement triggers.
